# DSA Scenario Guide - Real-Life Expectations

Each DSA entry explains the interview situation, why naive code fails, what to implement, and how to test it.

## Challenge Arrays & Hashing #1 - Two Sum
- File/folder: `DSA/Final_DSA_20_Questions_Per_Section.md`
- Function/code to work on: `solution function for Two Sum`
- Original ask: Pattern: HashMap lookup. Priority: P0.
- In simple words: Solve the named problem using the intended pattern, then explain the reasoning: Pattern: HashMap lookup. Priority: P0.
- Real-life scenario: In an interview or performance-heavy feature, you are asked to solve this pattern: Pattern: HashMap lookup. Priority: P0. The goal is to avoid a slow or fragile brute-force answer.
- What is going wrong: A naive approach may look fine on the first example but fail with large inputs, duplicates, empty data, or hidden edge cases.
- What needs to be corrected: Choose the intended pattern, code the optimized solution, then explain why it works and what the time and space costs are.
- Implementation checklist: State brute force, choose the optimized data structure, code the solution, dry-run an example, then verify time and space complexity.
- Expected output/result: An accepted solution that returns the problem required value, plus a short explanation of brute force, optimized approach, data structure, time complexity, space complexity, edge cases, and dry run.
- How to test: Run the sample cases from the platform, then add edge cases for empty input, one item, duplicates, negatives, or large values where relevant. Check both correctness and time complexity.
- You are done when: The solution passes sample cases, important edge cases, and the stated complexity is good enough for the intended constraints.
